<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Neighborhoods">Neighborhoods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Neighborhoods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Baltimore_neighborhoods" title="List of Baltimore neighborhoods">List of Baltimore neighborhoods</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Baltimore_neighborhoods_map.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3500" data-file-width="3090" height="396" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Baltimore_neighborhoods_map.png/350px-Baltimore_neighborhoods_map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Baltimore_neighborhoods_map.png/525px-Baltimore_neighborhoods_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Baltimore_neighborhoods_map.png/700px-Baltimore_neighborhoods_map.png 2x" width="350"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Baltimore_neighborhoods_map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A map of Baltimore with the official <a href="/wiki/List_of_Baltimore_neighborhoods" title="List of Baltimore neighborhoods">city-designated Baltimore neighborhoods</a>, by the Baltimore City Dept. of Planning</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Baltimore is officially divided into nine geographical regions: North, Northeast, East, Southeast, South, Southwest, West, Northwest, and Central, with each district patrolled by a respective <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Police_Department" title="Baltimore Police Department">Baltimore Police Department</a>. <a href="/wiki/Interstate_83" title="Interstate 83">Interstate 83</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Street_(Baltimore)" title="Charles Street (Baltimore)">Charles Street</a> down to <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Route_2" title="Maryland Route 2">Hanover Street</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ritchie_Highway" title="Ritchie Highway">Ritchie Highway</a> serve as the east-west dividing line and <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Route_150" title="Maryland Route 150">Eastern Avenue</a> to <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_40_in_Maryland" title="U.S. Route 40 in Maryland">Route 40</a> as the north-south dividing line. However, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore_Street" title="Baltimore Street">Baltimore Street</a> is north-south dividing line for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Postal_Service" title="U.S. Postal Service">U.S. Postal Service</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tilghman_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tilghman-100">[100]</a></sup> It is not uncommon for locals to divide the city simply by East or West Baltimore, using Charles Street or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/I-83" title="I-83">I-83</a> as a dividing line or into North and South using Baltimore Street as a dividing line.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Central_Baltimore">Central Baltimore</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Central Baltimore">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Central Baltimore, originally called the Middle District,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bpdhistory_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-bpdhistory-101">[101]</a></sup> stretches north of the <a href="/wiki/Inner_Harbor" title="Inner Harbor">Inner Harbor</a> up to the edge of <a href="/wiki/Druid_Hill_Park" title="Druid Hill Park">Druid Hill Park</a>. Downtown Baltimore has mainly served as a commercial district with limited residential opportunities. However, between 2000 and 2010, the downtown population grew 130 percent as old commercial properties have been replaced by residential property.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bernstein_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bernstein-102">[102]</a></sup> Still the city's main commercial area and business district, it includes Baltimore's sports complexes: <a href="/wiki/Oriole_Park_at_Camden_Yards" title="Oriole Park at Camden Yards">Oriole Park at Camden Yards</a>, <a href="/wiki/M%26T_Bank_Stadium" title="M&amp;T Bank Stadium">M&amp;T Bank Stadium</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore_Arena" title="Baltimore Arena">Baltimore Arena</a>; and the shops and attractions in the Inner Harbor: <a href="/wiki/Harborplace" title="Harborplace">Harborplace</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Convention_Center" title="Baltimore Convention Center">Baltimore Convention Center</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Aquarium_in_Baltimore" title="National Aquarium in Baltimore">National Aquarium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Science_Center" title="Maryland Science Center">Maryland Science Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pier_Six_Pavilion" title="Pier Six Pavilion">Pier Six Pavilion</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Power_Plant_Live" title="Power Plant Live">Power Plant Live</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tilghman_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-Tilghman-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland,_Baltimore" title="University of Maryland, Baltimore">University of Maryland, Baltimore</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland_Medical_Center" title="University of Maryland Medical Center">University of Maryland Medical Center</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lexington_Market" title="Lexington Market">Lexington Market</a> are also in the central district, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Hippodrome" title="Hippodrome">Hippodrome</a> and many nightclubs, bars, restaurants, shopping centers and various other attractions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tilghman_100-2"><a href="#cite_note-Tilghman-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bpdhistory_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-bpdhistory-101">[101]</a></sup> The northern portion of Central Baltimore, between downtown and the Druid Hill Park, is home to many of the city's cultural opportunities. <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Institute_College_of_Art" title="Maryland Institute College of Art">Maryland Institute College of Art</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Peabody_Institute" title="Peabody Institute">Peabody Institute</a> (music conservatory), <a href="/wiki/George_Peabody_Library" title="George Peabody Library">George Peabody Library</a>, <a href="/wiki/Enoch_Pratt_Free_Library" title="Enoch Pratt Free Library">Enoch Pratt Free Library</a> – Central Library, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lyric_Opera_House" title="Lyric Opera House">Lyric Opera House</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Meyerhoff_Symphony_Hall" title="Joseph Meyerhoff Symphony Hall">Joseph Meyerhoff Symphony Hall</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Walters_Art_Museum" title="Walters Art Museum">Walters Art Museum</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Historical_Society" title="Maryland Historical Society">Maryland Historical Society</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Enoch_Pratt" title="Enoch Pratt">Enoch Pratt</a> Mansion, and several galleries are located in this region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Baltimore">North Baltimore</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: North Baltimore">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1sherwoodgardens08.JPG"><img alt="Park and flowers at Sherwood Gardens, Guilford, Baltimore." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2056" data-file-width="2736" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/1sherwoodgardens08.JPG/220px-1sherwoodgardens08.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/1sherwoodgardens08.JPG/330px-1sherwoodgardens08.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/1sherwoodgardens08.JPG/440px-1sherwoodgardens08.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1sherwoodgardens08.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Sherwood_Gardens" title="Sherwood Gardens">Sherwood Gardens</a>, Guilford neighborhood, Baltimore</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>North Baltimore lies directly north of Central Baltimore and is bounded on the east by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Alameda_(Baltimore)" title="The Alameda (Baltimore)">The Alameda</a> and on the west by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pimlico_Road" title="Pimlico Road">Pimlico Road</a>. <a href="/wiki/Loyola_University_Maryland" title="Loyola University Maryland">Loyola University Maryland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Homewood_Campus_of_Johns_Hopkins_University" title="Homewood Campus of Johns Hopkins University">Johns Hopkins University Homewood Campus</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Mary%27s_Seminary_and_University" title="St. Mary's Seminary and University">St. Mary's Seminary and University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_of_Maryland_University" title="Notre Dame of Maryland University">Notre Dame of Maryland University</a> are located in this district. <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Polytechnic_Institute" title="Baltimore Polytechnic Institute">Baltimore Polytechnic Institute</a> high school for mathematics, science and engineering, and adjacent <a href="/wiki/Western_High_School_(Baltimore)" title="Western High School (Baltimore)">Western High School</a>, the oldest remaining public girls secondary school in America, share a joint campus at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cold_Spring_Lane" title="Cold Spring Lane">West Cold Spring Lane</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Route_25" title="Maryland Route 25">Falls Road</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Several historic and notable neighborhoods are in this district: <a href="/wiki/Roland_Park,_Baltimore" title="Roland Park, Baltimore">Roland Park</a> (1891), <a href="/wiki/Guilford,_Baltimore" title="Guilford, Baltimore">Guilford</a> (1913), <a href="/wiki/Homeland,_Baltimore" title="Homeland, Baltimore">Homeland</a> (1924), <a href="/wiki/Hampden,_Baltimore" title="Hampden, Baltimore">Hampden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Woodberry,_Baltimore" title="Woodberry, Baltimore">Woodberry</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Old_Goucher&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Old Goucher (page does not exist)">Old Goucher</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jones_Falls" title="Jones Falls">Jones Falls</a>. Along the <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Route_45" title="Maryland Route 45">York Road</a> corridor going north are the large neighborhoods of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles_Village" title="Charles Village">Charles Village</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waverly,_Baltimore" title="Waverly, Baltimore">Waverly</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mount_Washington,_Baltimore" title="Mount Washington, Baltimore">Mount Washington</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Station_North_Arts_and_Entertainment_District" title="Station North Arts and Entertainment District">Station North Arts and Entertainment District</a> is also located in North Baltimore.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Baltimore">South Baltimore</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: South Baltimore">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Federal_Hill_rowhouses.jpg"><img alt="Brick rowhouses with flags" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1623" data-file-width="2219" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Federal_Hill_rowhouses.jpg/220px-Federal_Hill_rowhouses.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Federal_Hill_rowhouses.jpg/330px-Federal_Hill_rowhouses.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Federal_Hill_rowhouses.jpg/440px-Federal_Hill_rowhouses.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Federal_Hill_rowhouses.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rowhouses, Federal Hill neighborhood, Baltimore</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>South Baltimore, a mixed industrial and residential area, consists of the "Old South Baltimore" peninsula below the Inner Harbor and east of the old <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/B%26O_Railroad" title="B&amp;O Railroad">B&amp;O Railroad</a>'s Camden line tracks and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russell_Street_(Baltimore)" title="Russell Street (Baltimore)">Russell Street</a> downtown. It is a culturally, ethnically, and socioeconomically diverse waterfront area with neighborhoods such as <a href="/wiki/Locust_Point,_Baltimore" title="Locust Point, Baltimore">Locust Point</a> and Riverside around a large park of the same name.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Locust_Point_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-Locust_Point-105">[105]</a></sup> Just south of the Inner Harbor, the historic <a href="/wiki/Federal_Hill,_Baltimore" title="Federal Hill, Baltimore">Federal Hill</a> neighborhood, is home to many working professionals, pubs and restaurants. At the end of the peninsula is historic <a href="/wiki/Fort_McHenry" title="Fort McHenry">Fort McHenry</a>, a National Park since the end of World War I, when the old U.S. Army Hospital surrounding the 1798 star-shaped battlements was torn down.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>The area south of the <a href="/wiki/Hanover_Street_Bridge" title="Hanover Street Bridge">Vietnam Veterans (Hanover Street) Bridge</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Patapsco_River" title="Patapsco River">Patapsco River</a> was annexed to the city in 1919 from being independent towns in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anne_Arundel_County" title="Anne Arundel County">Anne Arundel County</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Across the Hanover Street Bridge are residential areas such as <a href="/wiki/Cherry_Hill,_Baltimore" title="Cherry Hill, Baltimore">Cherry Hill</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn,_Baltimore" title="Brooklyn, Baltimore">Brooklyn</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Curtis_Bay,_Baltimore" title="Curtis Bay, Baltimore">Curtis Bay</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Fort_Armistead" title="Fort Armistead">Fort Armistead</a> bordering the city's south side from Anne Arundel County.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Northeast_Baltimore">Northeast Baltimore</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Northeast Baltimore">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Northeast is primarily a residential neighborhood, home to <a href="/wiki/Morgan_State_University" title="Morgan State University">Morgan State University</a>, bounded by the city line of 1919 on its northern and eastern boundaries, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sinclair_Lane" title="Sinclair Lane">Sinclair Lane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Route_151" title="Maryland Route 151">Erdman Avenue</a>, and <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_40_in_Maryland" title="U.S. Route 40 in Maryland">Pulaski Highway</a> to the south and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Alameda_(Baltimore)" title="The Alameda (Baltimore)">The Alameda</a> on to the west. Also in this wedge of the city on <a href="/wiki/33rd_Street_(Baltimore)" title="33rd Street (Baltimore)">33rd Street</a> is <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_City_College" title="Baltimore City College">Baltimore City College</a> high school, third oldest active public secondary school in the United States, founded downtown in 1839.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> Across <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loch_Raven_Boulevard" title="Loch Raven Boulevard">Loch Raven Boulevard</a> is the former site of the old <a href="/wiki/Memorial_Stadium_(Baltimore)" title="Memorial Stadium (Baltimore)">Memorial Stadium</a> for the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Indianapolis_Colts" title="History of the Indianapolis Colts">Baltimore Colts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">Baltimore Orioles</a>, now replaced by an <a href="/wiki/YMCA" title="YMCA">YMCA</a> athletic and housing complex.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Montebello&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lake Montebello (page does not exist)">Lake Montebello</a> is in Northeast Baltimore.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bpdhistory_101-2"><a href="#cite_note-bpdhistory-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="East_Baltimore">East Baltimore</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: East Baltimore">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Located below <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sinclair_Lane" title="Sinclair Lane">Sinclair Lane</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Route_151" title="Maryland Route 151">Erdman Avenue</a>, above <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orleans_Street_(Baltimore)" title="Orleans Street (Baltimore)">Orleans Street</a>, East Baltimore is mainly made up of residential neighborhoods. This section of East Baltimore is home to <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_Hospital" title="Johns Hopkins Hospital">Johns Hopkins Hospital</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University_School_of_Medicine" title="Johns Hopkins University School of Medicine">Johns Hopkins University School of Medicine</a> on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broadway_(Baltimore)" title="Broadway (Baltimore)">Broadway</a>. Notable neighborhoods include: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armistead_Gardens" title="Armistead Gardens">Armistead Gardens</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broadway_East" title="Broadway East">Broadway East</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barclay,_Baltimore" title="Barclay, Baltimore">Barclay</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ellwood_Park" title="Ellwood Park">Ellwood Park</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Greenmount,_Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Greenmount, Baltimore (page does not exist)">Greenmount</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roland_Park" title="Roland Park">Roland Park</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/McElderry_Park" title="McElderry Park">McElderry Park</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bpdhistory_101-3"><a href="#cite_note-bpdhistory-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>This area was the on-site film location for <i><a href="/wiki/Homicide:_Life_on_the_Street" title="Homicide: Life on the Street">Homicide: Life on the Street</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Corner" title="The Corner">The Corner</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wire" title="The Wire">The Wire</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Southeast_Baltimore">Southeast Baltimore</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Southeast Baltimore">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Southeast Baltimore, located below <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fayette_Street" title="Fayette Street">Fayette Street</a>, bordering the Inner Harbor and the Northwest Branch of the <a href="/wiki/Patapsco_River" title="Patapsco River">Patapsco River</a> to the west, the city line of 1919 on its eastern boundaries and the Patapsco River to the south, is a mixed industrial and residential area. <a href="/wiki/Patterson_Park" title="Patterson Park">Patterson Park</a>, the "Best Backyard in Baltimore,"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-collins2008_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-collins2008-113">[113]</a></sup> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Highlandtown_Arts_District,_Baltimore,_MD" title="Highlandtown Arts District, Baltimore, MD">Highlandtown Arts District</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_Bayview_Medical_Center" title="Johns Hopkins Bayview Medical Center">Johns Hopkins Bayview Medical Center</a> are located in Southeast Baltimore. The Shops at Canton Crossing opened in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Canton,_Baltimore" title="Canton, Baltimore">Canton</a> neighborhood, is located along Baltimore's prime waterfront. Other historic neighborhoods include: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fells_Point" title="Fells Point">Fells Point</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patterson_Park_(neighborhood),_Baltimore" title="Patterson Park (neighborhood), Baltimore">Patterson Park</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Butchers_Hill" title="Butchers Hill">Butchers Hill</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Highlandtown" title="Highlandtown">Highlandtown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greektown" title="Greektown">Greektown</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harbor_East" title="Harbor East">Harbor East</a>, <a href="/wiki/Little_Italy" title="Little Italy">Little Italy</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Upper_Fells_Point" title="Upper Fells Point">Upper Fells Point</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bpdhistory_101-4"><a href="#cite_note-bpdhistory-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Northwest_Baltimore">Northwest Baltimore</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Northwest Baltimore">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Northwestern is bounded by the county line to the north and west, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gwynns_Falls_Parkway" title="Gwynns Falls Parkway">Gwynns Falls Parkway</a> on the south and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pimlico_Road" title="Pimlico Road">Pimlico Road</a> on the east, is home to <a href="/wiki/Pimlico_Race_Course" title="Pimlico Race Course">Pimlico Race Course</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sinai_Hospital" title="Sinai Hospital">Sinai Hospital</a>, and the headquarters of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NAACP" title="NAACP">NAACP</a>. Its neighborhoods are mostly residential and are dissected by <a href="/wiki/Northern_Parkway_(Baltimore)" title="Northern Parkway (Baltimore)">Northern Parkway</a>. The area has been the center of Baltimore's Jewish community since after World War II. Notable neighborhoods include: <a href="/wiki/Pimlico,_Baltimore" title="Pimlico, Baltimore">Pimlico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mount_Washington,_Baltimore" title="Mount Washington, Baltimore">Mount Washington</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cheswolde,_Baltimore" title="Cheswolde, Baltimore">Cheswolde</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Park_Heights" title="Park Heights">Park Heights</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Park_Heights_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Park_Heights-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="West_Baltimore">West Baltimore</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: West Baltimore">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>West Baltimore is located west of downtown and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King,_Jr._Boulevard" title="Martin Luther King, Jr. Boulevard">Martin Luther King, Jr. Boulevard</a> and is bounded by Gwynns Falls Parkway, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fremont_Avenue" title="Fremont Avenue">Fremont Avenue</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore_Street" title="Baltimore Street">West Baltimore Street</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Old_West_Baltimore_Historic_District" title="Old West Baltimore Historic District">Old West Baltimore Historic District</a> includes the neighborhoods of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Harlem_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Harlem Park (page does not exist)">Harlem Park</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sandtown-Winchester" title="Sandtown-Winchester">Sandtown-Winchester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Druid_Heights" title="Druid Heights">Druid Heights</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madison_Park,_Baltimore" title="Madison Park, Baltimore">Madison Park</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Upton,_Baltimore" title="Upton, Baltimore">Upton</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nps_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-nps-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> Originally a predominantly German neighborhood, by the last half of the 1800s, Old West Baltimore was home to a substantial section of the city's African American population. It became the largest neighborhood for the city's black community and its cultural, political, and economic center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nps_116-1"><a href="#cite_note-nps-116">[116]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Coppin_State_University" title="Coppin State University">Coppin State University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mondawmin_Mall" title="Mondawmin Mall">Mondawmin Mall</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Edmondson,_Baltimore" title="Edmondson, Baltimore">Edmondson Village</a> are located in this district. The area's crime problems have provided subject material for television series, such as <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wire" title="The Wire">The Wire</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> Local organizations, such as the Sandtown Habitat for Humanity and the Upton Planning Committee, have been steadily transforming parts of formerly blighted areas of West Baltimore into clean, safe communities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Southwest_Baltimore">Southwest Baltimore</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Southwest Baltimore">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Southwest Baltimore is bound by the Baltimore County line to the west, West <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore_Street" title="Baltimore Street">Baltimore Street</a> to the north, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King_Jr._Boulevard_(Baltimore)" title="Martin Luther King Jr. Boulevard (Baltimore)">Martin Luther King Jr. Boulevard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baltimore%E2%80%93Washington_Parkway" title="Baltimore–Washington Parkway">Russell Street/Baltimore-Washington Parkway</a> (Maryland Route 295) to the east. Notable neighborhoods in Southwest Baltimore include: <a href="/wiki/Pigtown,_Baltimore" title="Pigtown, Baltimore">Pigtown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carrollton_Ridge,_Baltimore" title="Carrollton Ridge, Baltimore">Carrolton Ridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ridgely%27s_Delight,_Baltimore" title="Ridgely's Delight, Baltimore">Ridgely's Delight</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gwynns_Falls_Leakin_Park" title="Gwynns Falls Leakin Park">Leakin Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Violetville,_Baltimore" title="Violetville, Baltimore">Violetville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lakeland,_Baltimore" title="Lakeland, Baltimore">Lakeland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Morrell_Park,_Baltimore" title="Morrell Park, Baltimore">Morrell Park</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bpdhistory_101-5"><a href="#cite_note-bpdhistory-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/St._Agnes_Hospital_(Baltimore)" title="St. Agnes Hospital (Baltimore)">St. Agnes Hospital</a> on <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Route_372" title="Maryland Route 372">Wilkens</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caton_Avenue" title="Caton Avenue">Caton</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bpdhistory_101-6"><a href="#cite_note-bpdhistory-101">[101]</a></sup> avenues is located in this district with the neighboring <a href="/wiki/Cardinal_Gibbons_School_(Baltimore,_Maryland)" title="Cardinal Gibbons School (Baltimore, Maryland)">Cardinal Gibbons High School</a>, which is the former site of <a href="/wiki/Babe_Ruth" title="Babe Ruth">Babe Ruth</a>'s alma mater, St. Mary's Industrial School.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Also through this segment of Baltimore ran the beginnings of the historic <a href="/wiki/National_Road" title="National Road">National Road</a>, which was constructed beginning in 1806 along <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Frederick_Road" title="Old Frederick Road">Old Frederick Road</a> and continuing into the county on <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Route_144" title="Maryland Route 144">Frederick Road</a> into <a href="/wiki/Ellicott_City,_Maryland" title="Ellicott City, Maryland">Ellicott City, Maryland</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Other sides in this district are: <a href="/wiki/Mount_Clare_(Maryland)" title="Mount Clare (Maryland)">Carroll Park</a>, one of the city's largest parks, the colonial Mount Clare Mansion, and <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_1_in_Maryland" title="U.S. Route 1 in Maryland">Washington Boulevard</a>, which dates to pre-Revolutionary War days as the prime route out of the city to <a href="/wiki/Alexandria,_Virginia" title="Alexandria, Virginia">Alexandria, Virginia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_(Washington,_D.C.)" title="Georgetown (Washington, D.C.)">Georgetown</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Potomac_River" title="Potomac River">Potomac River</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adjacent_communities">Adjacent communities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Adjacent communities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_classification" title="Köppen classification">Köppen classification</a>, Baltimore lies within the <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a> zone (<i>Cfa</i>), with four distinct seasons, and is part of USDA plant hardiness zones 7b and 8a.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Winters are chilly but variable, with sporadic snowfall: January has a daily average of 35.8 °F (2.1 °C),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_downtown_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA_downtown-122">[122]</a></sup> though temperatures reach 50 °F (10 °C) rather often and drop below 20 °F (−7 °C) when Arctic air masses affect the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_downtown_122-1"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA_downtown-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>The average seasonal snowfall is 20.1 inches (51 cm),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_NowData_2_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA_NowData_2-123">[123]</a></sup> but it varies greatly depending on the winter, with some seasons seeing minimal snow while others see several major <a href="/wiki/Nor%27easter" title="Nor'easter">Nor'easters</a>. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[a]</a></sup> Due to lessened <a href="/wiki/Urban_heat_island" title="Urban heat island">urban heat island</a> (UHI) as compared to the <a href="/wiki/City_limits" title="City limits">city proper</a> and distance from the moderating Chesapeake Bay, the outlying and inland parts of the Baltimore metro area are usually cooler, especially at night, than the city proper and the coastal towns. Thus, in the northern and western suburbs, winter snowfall is more significant, and some areas average more than 30 in (76 cm) of snow per winter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup> It is by no means uncommon for the rain-snow line to set up in the metro area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Freezing_rain" title="Freezing rain">Freezing rain</a> and sleet occurs a few times each winter in the area, as warm air overrides cold air at the low to mid-levels of the atmosphere. When the wind blows from the east, the cold air gets <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cold_air_damming" title="Cold air damming">dammed against the mountains</a> to the west and the result is freezing rain or sleet.</p>
<p>Spring and autumn are warm, with spring being the wettest season in terms of the number of precipitation days. Summers are hot and humid with a daily average in July of 80.7 °F (27.1 °C),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_downtown_122-2"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA_downtown-122">[122]</a></sup> and the combination of heat and humidity leads to rather frequent thunderstorms. A southeasterly bay breeze off the Chesapeake often occurs on summer afternoons when hot air rises over inland areas; prevailing winds from the southwest interacting with this breeze as well as the city proper's UHI can seriously exacerbate air quality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup> In late summer and early autumn the track of hurricanes or their remnants may cause flooding in downtown Baltimore, despite the city being far removed from the typical coastal <a href="/wiki/Storm_surge" title="Storm surge">storm surge</a> areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Baltimore_Weather.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="123" data-file-width="615" height="44" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Baltimore_Weather.jpg/220px-Baltimore_Weather.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Baltimore_Weather.jpg/330px-Baltimore_Weather.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Baltimore_Weather.jpg/440px-Baltimore_Weather.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Baltimore_Weather.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Humidity can produce dramatic lightning storms over the Baltimore area.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Extreme temperatures range from −7 °F (−22 °C) on February 9, 1934, and <a href="/wiki/Great_Blizzard_of_1899" title="Great Blizzard of 1899">February 10, 1899</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[b]</a></sup> up to 108 °F (42 °C) on July 22, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[131]</a></sup> On average, 100 °F (38 °C)+ temperatures occur on 0.9 days annually, 90 °F (32 °C)+ on 37 days, and there are 10 days where the high fails to reach the freezing mark.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_downtown_122-3"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA_downtown-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>|Jan record high F = 77 |Feb record high F = 83 |Mar record high F = 87 |Apr record high F = 94 |May record high F = 100 |Jun record high F = 110 |Jul record high F = 108 |Aug record high F = 107 |Sep record high F = 103 |Oct record high F = 96 |Nov record high F = 86 |Dec record high F = 79 |year record high F = 110 |Jan record low F = -6 |Feb record low F = -9 |Mar record low F = 0 |Apr record low F = 14 |May record low F = 32 |Jun record low F = 38 |Jul record low F = 49 |Aug record low F = 45 |Sep record low F = 35 |Oct record low F = 26 |Nov record low F = 12 |Dec record low F = -3</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

1990–2000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[139]</a></sup> 2010–2015<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QuickFacts_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-QuickFacts-143">[140]</a></sup></td>

<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 Census</a><sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 620,961 people living in Baltimore City in 242,268 households. The population decreased by 4.6% since the 2000 Census. Among school-age children between 5–17 years old, there was a 23% decline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sherman2015_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-sherman2015-144">[141]</a></sup> Baltimore's population has declined at each census since its peak in 1950.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bernstein_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bernstein-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2011, then-Mayor <a href="/wiki/Stephanie_Rawlings-Blake" title="Stephanie Rawlings-Blake">Stephanie Rawlings-Blake</a> said her main goal was to increase the city's population by improving city services to reduce the number of people leaving the city and by passing legislation protecting immigrants' rights to stimulate growth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sherman2015_144-1"><a href="#cite_note-sherman2015-144">[141]</a></sup> For the first time in decades, in July 2012, the U.S. Census Bureau's census estimate showed the population grew by 1,100 residents, a 0.2% increase from the previous year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kilar2013_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-kilar2013-145">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Gentrification" title="Gentrification">Gentrification</a> has also increased since the 2000 census, primarily in East Baltimore, downtown, and Central Baltimore.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-litten2015_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-litten2015-146">[143]</a></sup> Downtown Baltimore and its surrounding neighborhoods are seeing a resurgence of young professionals and immigrants, mirroring major cities across the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kilar2013_145-1"><a href="#cite_note-kilar2013-145">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, Baltimore was the second city in the United States to reach a population of 100,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1850_Fast_Facts_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-1850_Fast_Facts-148">[145]</a></sup> From the 1830 through 1850 U.S. censuses, Baltimore was the second most-populous city,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1850_Fast_Facts_148-1"><a href="#cite_note-1850_Fast_Facts-148">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[146]</a></sup> before being surpassed by Philadelphia in 1860.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[147]</a></sup> It was among the top 10 cities in population in the United States in every census up to the 1980 census,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[148]</a></sup> and after World War II had a population of nearly a million.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Characteristics">Characteristics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Characteristics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Baltimore" title="Ethnic groups in Baltimore">Ethnic groups in Baltimore</a></div>

<p>According to the 2010 Census<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Baltimore's population is 63.7% Black, 29.6% White, 2.3% Asian, and 0.4%, American Indian and Alaska Native. Across races, 4.2% of the population are of <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Hispanics_and_Latinos_in_Baltimore" title="History of the Hispanics and Latinos in Baltimore">Hispanic, Latino, or Spanish origin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QuickFacts_143-1"><a href="#cite_note-QuickFacts-143">[140]</a></sup> Females made up 53.4% of the population. The median age was 35 years old, with 22.4% under 18 years old, 65.8% from 18 to 64 years old, and 11.8% 65 or older.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QuickFacts_143-2"><a href="#cite_note-QuickFacts-143">[140]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2005, approximately 30,778 people (6.5%) identified as <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">gay, lesbian, or bisexual</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GLB_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-GLB-153">[150]</a></sup> In 2012, <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_Maryland" title="Same-sex marriage in Maryland">same-sex marriage in Maryland</a> was legalized, going into effect January 1, 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[151]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Income_and_housing">Income and housing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Income and housing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2009, the median household income was $42,241 and the median income per capita was $25,707, compared to the national median income of $53,889 per household and $28,930 per capita. In Baltimore, 23.7% of the population lived below the poverty line, compared to 13.5% nationwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QuickFacts_143-3"><a href="#cite_note-QuickFacts-143">[140]</a></sup></p>
<p>Housing in Baltimore is relatively inexpensive for large, coastal cities of its size. The median sale price for homes in Baltimore in 2012 was $95,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[152]</a></sup> Despite the housing collapse, and along with the national trends, Baltimore residents still face slowly increasing rent (up 3% in the summer of 2010).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-name_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-name-156">[153]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Homelessness" title="Homelessness">homeless</a> population in Baltimore is steadily increasing; it exceeded 4,000 people in 2011. The increase in the number of young homeless people was particularly severe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CP-homelessness-19Oct2011_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-CP-homelessness-19Oct2011-157">[154]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Baltimore_Basilica,_Baltimore,_Maryland.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3402" data-file-width="4568" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Baltimore_Basilica%2C_Baltimore%2C_Maryland.JPG/220px-Baltimore_Basilica%2C_Baltimore%2C_Maryland.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Baltimore_Basilica%2C_Baltimore%2C_Maryland.JPG/330px-Baltimore_Basilica%2C_Baltimore%2C_Maryland.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Baltimore_Basilica%2C_Baltimore%2C_Maryland.JPG/440px-Baltimore_Basilica%2C_Baltimore%2C_Maryland.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Baltimore_Basilica,_Baltimore,_Maryland.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore_Basilica" title="Baltimore Basilica">Baltimore Basilica</a>, the first cathedral built in the U.S.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A little under half (47%) of people in Baltimore report affiliating with a religion. Catholicism is the largest religious affiliation, comprising 12% percent of the population, followed by the Baptist Church (7%), then Judaism (4.3%). Around 11.4% identify with other Christian denominations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[155]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[156]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As of 2010, 91% (526,705) of Baltimore residents five years old and older spoke only English at home. Close to 4% (21,661) spoke Spanish. Other languages, such as <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Africa" title="Languages of Africa">African languages</a>, French, and Chinese are spoken by less than 1% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[157]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">Crime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Crime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Baltimore" title="Crime in Baltimore">Crime in Baltimore</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2016-05-11_18_45_30_Baltimore_City_Police_Car_at_the_intersection_of_Franklin_Street_(U.S._Route_40)_and_Franklintown_Road_in_Baltimore_City,_Maryland.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/2016-05-11_18_45_30_Baltimore_City_Police_Car_at_the_intersection_of_Franklin_Street_%28U.S._Route_40%29_and_Franklintown_Road_in_Baltimore_City%2C_Maryland.jpg/220px-2016-05-11_18_45_30_Baltimore_City_Police_Car_at_the_intersection_of_Franklin_Street_%28U.S._Route_40%29_and_Franklintown_Road_in_Baltimore_City%2C_Maryland.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/2016-05-11_18_45_30_Baltimore_City_Police_Car_at_the_intersection_of_Franklin_Street_%28U.S._Route_40%29_and_Franklintown_Road_in_Baltimore_City%2C_Maryland.jpg/330px-2016-05-11_18_45_30_Baltimore_City_Police_Car_at_the_intersection_of_Franklin_Street_%28U.S._Route_40%29_and_Franklintown_Road_in_Baltimore_City%2C_Maryland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/2016-05-11_18_45_30_Baltimore_City_Police_Car_at_the_intersection_of_Franklin_Street_%28U.S._Route_40%29_and_Franklintown_Road_in_Baltimore_City%2C_Maryland.jpg/440px-2016-05-11_18_45_30_Baltimore_City_Police_Car_at_the_intersection_of_Franklin_Street_%28U.S._Route_40%29_and_Franklintown_Road_in_Baltimore_City%2C_Maryland.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2016-05-11_18_45_30_Baltimore_City_Police_Car_at_the_intersection_of_Franklin_Street_(U.S._Route_40)_and_Franklintown_Road_in_Baltimore_City,_Maryland.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Patrol car of the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Police_Department" title="Baltimore Police Department">Baltimore Police Department</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Crime in Baltimore, generally concentrated in areas high in poverty, has been above the national average for many years. Overall reported crime has dropped by 60% from the mid 1990s to the mid 2010s, but homicide rates remain high and exceed the national average. The worst years for crime in Baltimore overall were from 1993–1996; 1995, with 96,243 crimes reported in 1995 (compare with 38,321 in 2014, albeit following a population decline of 100,000). Baltimore's 344 homicides in 2015 represented the highest homicide rate in the city's recorded history—52.5 per 100,000 people, surpassing the record set in 1993—and the second-highest for U.S. cities behind <a href="/wiki/St._Louis" title="St. Louis">St. Louis</a> and ahead of Detroit. To put that in perspective, New York City, a city with a 2015 population of 8,491,079 recorded a total of 339 homicides in 2015. Baltimore is a city with a 2015 population of 621,849; which means that in 2015 Baltimore had a homicide rate 14 times higher than New York City's. Of Baltimore's 344 homicides in 2015, 321 (93.3%) of the victims were African-American (in a city in which the African-American demographic is 63% of the population).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Chicago, which saw 762 homicides in 2016 compared to Baltimore's 318, still had a homicide rate (27.2) that was half of Baltimore's because Chicago has a population 4 times greater than Baltimore's.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Drug use and deaths by drug use (particularly drugs used intravenously, such as heroin) are a related problem which has crippled Baltimore for decades. Among cities greater than 400,000, Baltimore ranked 2nd in its opiate drug death rate in the United States behind Dayton, Ohio. The DEA reported that a staggering 10% of Baltimore's population- about 64,000 people- are addicted to heroin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[158]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[160]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[161]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[162]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2011, Baltimore police reported 196 homicides, the lowest number in the city since a count of 197 homicides in 1978 and far lower than the peak homicide count of 353 slayings in 1993. City leaders at the time credited a sustained focus on repeat violent offenders and increased community engagement for the continued drop, reflecting a nationwide decline in crime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[163]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[164]</a></sup></p>
<p>On August 8, 2014, Baltimore's new youth <a href="/wiki/Curfew" title="Curfew">curfew</a> law went into effect. It prohibits unaccompanied children under age 14 from being on the streets after 9 p.m. and those aged 14–16 from being out after 10 p.m. during the week and 11 p.m. on weekends and during the summer. The goal is to keep children out of dangerous places and reduce crime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[165]</a></sup></p>
<p>Crime in Baltimore reached another peak in 2015 when the year's tally of 344 homicides was second only to the record 353 in 1993, when Baltimore had about 100,000 more residents. The killings in 2015 were on pace with recent years in the early months of 2015 but skyrocketed after the unrest and rioting of late April. In five of the next eight months, killings topped 30 or 40 a month. Nearly 90 percent of 2015's homicides were the result of shootings, renewing calls for new gun laws. Counting nonfatal shootings, gun violence was up more than 75 percent compared to 2014, with more than 900 people shot.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 2016, according to annual crime statistics released by the Baltimore Police Department, there were 318 murders in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[166]</a></sup> This total marked a 7.56 percent decline in homicides from 2015.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Once a predominantly industrial town, with an economic base focused on steel processing, shipping, auto manufacturing (General Motors <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Assembly" title="Baltimore Assembly">Baltimore Assembly</a>), and transportation, the city experienced <a href="/wiki/Deindustrialization" title="Deindustrialization">deindustrialization</a> which cost residents tens of thousands of low-skill, high-wage jobs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vicino_2008_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vicino_2008-170">[167]</a></sup> The city now relies on a low-wage <a href="/wiki/Service_economy" title="Service economy">service economy</a>, which accounts for 31% of jobs in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[168]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[169]</a></sup> Around the turn of the century, Baltimore was the leading US manufacturer of <a href="/wiki/Rye_whiskey" title="Rye whiskey">rye whiskey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Straw_hat" title="Straw hat">straw hats</a>. It also led in refining of crude oil, brought to the city by pipeline from Pennsylvania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[170]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of March 2015 the U.S. Bureau of Labor Statistics calculates Baltimore's unemployment rate at 8.1%<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[171]</a></sup> while one quarter of Baltimore residents (and 37% of Baltimore children) live in poverty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kilar_.E2.80.93_20_Sept_2012_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kilar_.E2.80.93_20_Sept_2012-175">[172]</a></sup> The 2012 closure of a major steel plant at Sparrows Point is expected to have a further impact on employment and the local economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[173]</a></sup> The Census Bureau reported in 2013 that 207,000 workers commute into Baltimore city each day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[174]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Baltimore" title="Downtown Baltimore">Downtown Baltimore</a> is the primary economic asset within Baltimore City and the region with 29.1 million square feet of office space. The tech sector is rapidly growing as the Baltimore metro ranks 8th in the CBRE Tech Talent Report among 50 U.S. metro areas for high growth rate and number of tech professionals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[175]</a></sup> <i>Forbes</i> ranked Baltimore fourth among America's "new tech hot spots".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[176]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:1108px;">

</div>
<p>The city is home to the <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_Hospital" title="Johns Hopkins Hospital">Johns Hopkins Hospital</a>. Other large <a href="/wiki/Category:Companies_based_in_Baltimore" title="Category:Companies based in Baltimore">companies in Baltimore</a> include <a href="/wiki/Under_Armour" title="Under Armour">Under Armour</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UA_HQ_2011_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-UA_HQ_2011-180">[177]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cordish_Company" title="Cordish Company">Cordish Company</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[178]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Legg_Mason" title="Legg Mason">Legg Mason</a>, <a href="/wiki/McCormick_%26_Company" title="McCormick &amp; Company">McCormick &amp; Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/T._Rowe_Price" title="T. Rowe Price">T. Rowe Price</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Farms" title="Royal Farms">Royal Farms</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[179]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Sugar_refinery" title="Sugar refinery">sugar refinery</a> owned by <a href="/wiki/American_Sugar_Refining" title="American Sugar Refining">American Sugar Refining</a> is one of Baltimore's cultural icons. Nonprofits based in Baltimore include <a href="/wiki/Lutheran_Services_in_America" title="Lutheran Services in America">Lutheran Services in America</a> and <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Relief_Services" title="Catholic Relief Services">Catholic Relief Services</a>.</p>
<p>Almost a quarter of the jobs in the Baltimore region were in science, technology, engineering and math as of mid 2013, in part attributed to the city's extensive undergraduate and graduate schools; maintenance and repair experts were included in this count.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bizjournal_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-bizjournal-183">[180]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Port">Port</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Port">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The center of international commerce for the region is the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_World_Trade_Center" title="Baltimore World Trade Center">World Trade Center Baltimore</a>. It houses the Maryland Port Administration and U.S. headquarters for major shipping lines. Baltimore is ranked 9th for total dollar value of cargo and 13th for cargo tonnage for all U.S. ports. In 2014, total cargo moving through the port totaled 29.5 million tons, down from 30.3 million tons in 2013. The value of cargo traveling through the port in 2014 came to $52.5 billion, down from $52.6 billion in 2013. The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Baltimore" title="Port of Baltimore">Port of Baltimore</a> generates $3 billion in annual wages and salary, as well as supporting 14,630 direct jobs and 108,000 jobs connected to port work. In 2014, the port also generated more than $300 million in taxes. It serves over 50 ocean carriers making nearly 1,800 annual visits. Among all U.S. ports, Baltimore is first in handling automobiles, light trucks, farm and construction machinery; and imported forest products, aluminum, and sugar. The port is second in coal exports. The Port of Baltimore's cruise industry, which offers year-round trips on several lines supports over 500 jobs and brings in over $90 million to Maryland's economy annually. Growth at the port continues with the Maryland Port Administration plans to turn the southern tip of the former steel mill into a marine terminal, primarily for car and truck shipments, but also for anticipated new business coming to Baltimore after the completion of the <a href="/wiki/Panama_Canal_expansion_project" title="Panama Canal expansion project">Panama Canal expansion project</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[181]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Baltimore's history and attractions have allowed the city to become a strong tourist destination on the East Coast. In 2014, the city hosted 24.5 million visitors, who spent $5.2 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[182]</a></sup> The Baltimore Visitor Center, which is operated by <a href="/wiki/Visit_Baltimore" title="Visit Baltimore">Visit Baltimore</a>, is located on Light Street in the <a href="/wiki/Inner_Harbor" title="Inner Harbor">Inner Harbor</a>. Much of the city's tourism centers around the Inner Harbor, with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Aquarium_in_Baltimore" title="National Aquarium in Baltimore">National Aquarium</a> being Maryland's top tourist destination. Baltimore Harbor's restoration has made it "a city of boats", with several historic ships and other attractions on display and open for the public to visit. The <a href="/wiki/USS_Constellation_(1854)" title="USS Constellation (1854)">USS <i>Constellation</i></a>, the last Civil War-era vessel afloat, is docked at the head of the Inner Harbor; the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USS_Torsk_(SS-423)" title="USS Torsk (SS-423)">USS <i>Torsk</i></a>, a submarine that holds the Navy's record for dives (more than 10,000); and the Coast Guard cutter <i><a href="/wiki/USCGC_Taney_(WHEC-37)" title="USCGC Taney (WHEC-37)">Taney</a></i>, the last surviving U.S. warship that was in <a href="/wiki/Pearl_Harbor" title="Pearl Harbor">Pearl Harbor</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">Japanese attack</a> on December 7, 1941, and which engaged Japanese Zero aircraft during the battle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-soundingsonline.com_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-soundingsonline.com-186">[183]</a></sup></p>
<p>Also docked is the lightship <i>Chesapeake</i>, which for decades marked the entrance to Chesapeake Bay; and the Seven Foot Knoll Lighthouse, the oldest surviving <a href="/wiki/Screw-pile_lighthouse" title="Screw-pile lighthouse">screw-pile lighthouse</a> on Chesapeake Bay, which once marked the mouth of the Patapsco River and the entrance to Baltimore. All of these attractions are owned and maintained by the <a href="/wiki/Historic_Ships_in_Baltimore" title="Historic Ships in Baltimore">Historic Ships in Baltimore</a> organization. The Inner Harbor also is the home port of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pride_of_Baltimore_II" title="Pride of Baltimore II">Pride of Baltimore II</a></i>, the state of Maryland's "goodwill ambassador" ship, a reconstruction of a famous <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Clipper" title="Baltimore Clipper">Baltimore Clipper</a> ship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-soundingsonline.com_186-1"><a href="#cite_note-soundingsonline.com-186">[183]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other popular tourist destinations throughout the city include <a href="/wiki/Oriole_Park_at_Camden_Yards" title="Oriole Park at Camden Yards">Oriole Park at Camden Yards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fort_McHenry" title="Fort McHenry">Fort McHenry</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mount_Vernon,_Baltimore" title="Mount Vernon, Baltimore">Mount Vernon</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fells_Point" title="Fells Point">Fells Point</a> neighborhoods, and museums such as the <a href="/wiki/Walters_Art_Museum" title="Walters Art Museum">Walters Art Museum</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Museum_of_Industry" title="Baltimore Museum of Industry">Baltimore Museum of Industry</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/B%26O_Railroad_Museum" title="B&amp;O Railroad Museum">B&amp;O Railroad Museum</a>.</p>
<p>Baltimore, and more specifically, the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Convention_Center" title="Baltimore Convention Center">Baltimore Convention Center</a> is home to <a href="/wiki/BronyCon" title="BronyCon">BronyCon</a>, the world's largest convention for fans of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/My_Little_Pony:_Friendship_is_Magic" title="My Little Pony: Friendship is Magic">My Little Pony: Friendship is Magic</a>. The convention had over 6,300 attendees in 2017, and 10,011 attendees during its peak in 2015.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>

<p>Baltimore is the home of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Aquarium_in_Baltimore" title="National Aquarium in Baltimore">National Aquarium</a>, one of the world's largest.</p>
