<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Baltimore" title="Culture of Baltimore">Culture of Baltimore</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Baltimore" title="List of people from Baltimore">List of people from Baltimore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Baltimore" title="Music of Baltimore">Music of Baltimore</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_in_Baltimore" title="List of museums in Baltimore">List of museums in Baltimore</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Converted.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1254" data-file-width="930" height="229" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c1/Converted.png/170px-Converted.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c1/Converted.png/255px-Converted.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c1/Converted.png/340px-Converted.png 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Converted.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Washington Monument</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Historically a working-class port town, Baltimore has sometimes been dubbed a "city of neighborhoods", with 72 designated historic districts<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[184]</a></sup> traditionally occupied by distinct ethnic groups. Most notable today are three downtown areas along the port: the Inner Harbor, frequented by tourists due to its hotels, shops, and museums; Fells Point, once a favorite entertainment spot for sailors but now refurbished and gentrified (and featured in the movie <i><a href="/wiki/Sleepless_in_Seattle" title="Sleepless in Seattle">Sleepless in Seattle</a></i>); and <a href="/wiki/Little_Italy,_Baltimore" title="Little Italy, Baltimore">Little Italy</a>, located between the other two, where Baltimore's Italian-American community is based – and where former U.S. House Speaker <a href="/wiki/Nancy_Pelosi" title="Nancy Pelosi">Nancy Pelosi</a> grew up. Further inland, <a href="/wiki/Mount_Vernon,_Baltimore" title="Mount Vernon, Baltimore">Mount Vernon</a> is the traditional center of cultural and artistic life of the city; it is home to a distinctive <a href="/wiki/Washington_Monument_(Baltimore)" title="Washington Monument (Baltimore)">Washington Monument</a>, set atop a hill in a 19th-century urban square, that predates the more well-known monument in Washington, D.C. by several decades. Baltimore also has a significant <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Germans_in_Baltimore" title="History of the Germans in Baltimore">German American</a> population,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[185]</a></sup> and was the second largest port of immigration to the United States, behind <a href="/wiki/Ellis_Island" title="Ellis Island">Ellis Island</a> in New York and New Jersey. Between 1820 and 1989, almost 2 million who were German, <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Poles_in_Baltimore" title="History of the Poles in Baltimore">Polish</a>, English, Irish, <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Russians_in_Baltimore" title="History of the Russians in Baltimore">Russian</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Lithuanians_in_Baltimore" title="History of the Lithuanians in Baltimore">Lithuanian</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_French_in_Baltimore" title="History of the French in Baltimore">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Ukrainians_in_Baltimore" title="History of the Ukrainians in Baltimore">Ukrainian</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Czechs_in_Baltimore" title="History of the Czechs in Baltimore">Czech</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Greeks_in_Baltimore" title="History of the Greeks in Baltimore">Greek</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Italians_in_Baltimore" title="History of the Italians in Baltimore">Italian</a> came to Baltimore, most between the years 1861 to 1930. By 1913, when Baltimore was averaging forty thousand immigrants per year, World War I closed off the flow of immigrants. By 1970, Baltimore's heyday as an immigration center was a distant memory. There also was a <a href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Baltimore" title="Chinatown, Baltimore">Chinatown</a> dating back to at least the 1880s which consisted of no more than 400 Chinese residents. A local Chinese-American association remains based there, but only one Chinese restaurant as of 2009.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BromoSeltzertowerBaltimore.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3521" data-file-width="2848" height="247" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/BromoSeltzertowerBaltimore.jpg/200px-BromoSeltzertowerBaltimore.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/BromoSeltzertowerBaltimore.jpg/300px-BromoSeltzertowerBaltimore.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/BromoSeltzertowerBaltimore.jpg/400px-BromoSeltzertowerBaltimore.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BromoSeltzertowerBaltimore.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Emerson_Bromo-Seltzer_Tower" title="Emerson Bromo-Seltzer Tower">Emerson Bromo-Seltzer Tower</a>, built in 1911. The 15 stories of the Bromo Seltzer Tower have been transformed into studio spaces for visual and literary artists</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Baltimore has quite a history when it comes to making beer, an art that thrived in Baltimore from the 1800s to the 1950s with over 100 old breweries in the city's past.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[186]</a></sup> The best remaining example of that history is the old <a href="/wiki/American_Brewery_(building)" title="American Brewery (building)">American Brewery Building</a> on North Gay Street and the <a href="/wiki/National_Brewing_Company" title="National Brewing Company">National Brewing Company</a> building in the <a href="/wiki/Brewers_Hill" title="Brewers Hill">Brewer's Hill</a> neighborhood. In the 1940s the National Brewing Company introduced the nation's first six-pack. National's two most prominent brands, were <a href="/wiki/National_Bohemian" title="National Bohemian">National Bohemian</a> Beer colloquially "Natty Boh" and <a href="/wiki/Colt_45_(malt_liquor)" title="Colt 45 (malt liquor)">Colt 45</a>. Listed on the <a href="/wiki/Pabst_Brewing_Company" title="Pabst Brewing Company">Pabst</a> website as a "Fun Fact", Colt 45 was named after running back <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Hill_(American_football)" title="Jerry Hill (American football)">#45 Jerry Hill</a> of the 1963 <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis_Colts#The_NFL_Baltimore_Colts" title="Indianapolis Colts">Baltimore Colts</a> and not the <a href="/wiki/.45_Colt" title=".45 Colt">.45 caliber handgun ammunition round</a>. Both brands are still made today and served all around the Baltimore area at bars, Oriole and Ravens games. The Natty Boh logo appears on all cans, bottles, and packaging; and merchandise featuring him can still easily be found in shops in Maryland, including several in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fells_Point" title="Fells Point">Fells Point</a>.</p>
<p>Each year the <a href="/wiki/Artscape_(festival)" title="Artscape (festival)">Artscape</a> takes place in the city in the <a href="/wiki/Bolton_Hill,_Baltimore" title="Bolton Hill, Baltimore">Bolton Hill</a> neighborhood, due to its proximity to Maryland Institute College of Art. Artscape styles itself as the "largest free arts festival in America".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[187]</a></sup> Each May, the <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Film_Festival" title="Maryland Film Festival">Maryland Film Festival</a> takes place in Baltimore, using all five screens of the historic <a href="/wiki/Charles_Theatre" title="Charles Theatre">Charles Theatre</a> as its anchor venue. Many movies and television shows have been filmed in Baltimore. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wire" title="The Wire">The Wire</a></i> was set and filmed in Baltimore. <i><a href="/wiki/House_of_Cards_(U.S._TV_series)" title="House of Cards (U.S. TV series)">House of Cards</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Veep" title="Veep">Veep</a></i> are set in Washington, D.C. but filmed in Baltimore.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[188]</a></sup></p>
<p>Baltimore has cultural museums in many areas of study. <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Museum_of_Art" title="Baltimore Museum of Art">The Baltimore Museum of Art</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Walters_Art_Museum" title="Walters Art Museum">Walters Art Museum</a> are internationally renowned for its collection of art. The Baltimore Museum of Art has the largest holding of works by <a href="/wiki/Henri_Matisse" title="Henri Matisse">Henri Matisse</a> in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[189]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/National_Great_Blacks_In_Wax_Museum" title="National Great Blacks In Wax Museum">National Great Blacks in Wax Museum</a> is the first African American wax museum in the country, featuring more than 150 life-size and lifelike wax figures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-firsts_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-firsts-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Baltimore is known for its Maryland <a href="/wiki/Callinectes_sapidus" title="Callinectes sapidus">blue crabs</a>, crab cake, <a href="/wiki/Old_Bay_Seasoning" title="Old Bay Seasoning">Old Bay Seasoning</a>, pit beef, and the "chicken box." The city has many restaurants in or around the Inner Harbor. The most known and acclaimed are the Charleston, Woodberry Kitchen, and the <a href="/wiki/Duff_Goldman" title="Duff Goldman">Charm City Cakes</a> bakery featured on the Food Network's <a href="/wiki/Ace_of_Cakes" title="Ace of Cakes">Ace of Cakes</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Little_Italy,_Baltimore" title="Little Italy, Baltimore">Little Italy</a> neighborhood's biggest draw is the food. Fells Point also is a foodie neighborhood for tourists and locals and is where the oldest continuously running tavern in the country, "The Horse You Came In On Saloon," is located.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[190]</a></sup> Many of the city's upscale restaurants can be found in <a href="/wiki/Inner_Harbor_East,_Baltimore" title="Inner Harbor East, Baltimore">Harbor East</a>. Five public markets are located across the city. The <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Public_Markets" title="Baltimore Public Markets">Baltimore Public Market System</a> is the oldest continuously operating public market system in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[191]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lexington_Market" title="Lexington Market">Lexington Market</a> is one of the longest-running markets in the world and longest running in the country, having been around since 1782. The market continues to stand at its original site. Baltimore is the last place in America where one can still find <a href="/wiki/Arabber" title="Arabber">arabbers</a>, vendors who sell fresh fruits and vegetables from a horse-drawn cart that goes up and down neighborhood streets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[192]</a></sup> Food- and drink-rating site Zagat ranked Baltimore second in a list of the 17 best food cities in the country in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[193]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_dialect">Local dialect</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Local dialect">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore_dialect" title="Baltimore dialect">Baltimore dialect</a></div>
<p>One thing visitors quickly notice is that some locals refer to their city as "Balmer", dropping the "t". The traditional local accent, particular to some working-class areas of the city, has long been noted and celebrated as "Baltimorese" or "Bawlmorese". While in other parts of the city, locals refer to their city as "Baldamore". Baltimore's dialect is a member of the Atlantic midland English dialect group, and shares many characteristics with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philadelphia_accent" title="Philadelphia accent">Philadelphia</a>'s, such as the addition of an "eh" sound before a long "o". Its influence distinguishes Baltimore, especially with words containing "oi" flattened into an "aw" sound.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[194]</a></sup> The Baltimore accent, however is noted for sounding more southern than Philadelphia's. Glide deletion in the accent is present, with the long "i" sound being flattened to "ah" among certain speakers before voiced, liquid and nasal consonants. Due to its combination of <a href="/wiki/Rhoticity_in_English" title="Rhoticity in English">rhoticity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Semivowel" title="Semivowel">glide</a> deletion, the word "iron" is pronounced somewhat like "arn" and the word "fire" like "far".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Baltimore native <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Waters_(director_born_1946)" title="John Waters (director born 1946)">John Waters</a> parodies the city and its dialect extensively in his films. Most of them are filmed and/or set in Baltimore, including the 1972 cult classic <i><a href="/wiki/Pink_Flamingos" title="Pink Flamingos">Pink Flamingos</a></i>, as well as <i><a href="/wiki/Hairspray_(1988_film)" title="Hairspray (1988 film)">Hairspray</a></i> and its <a href="/wiki/Hairspray_(musical)" title="Hairspray (musical)">Broadway musical remake</a>.</p>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_films_shot_in_Baltimore" title="List of films shot in Baltimore">List of films shot in Baltimore</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Performing_arts">Performing arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Performing arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hippodrome_Baltimore.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3240" data-file-width="4320" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Hippodrome_Baltimore.JPG/220px-Hippodrome_Baltimore.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Hippodrome_Baltimore.JPG/330px-Hippodrome_Baltimore.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Hippodrome_Baltimore.JPG/440px-Hippodrome_Baltimore.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hippodrome_Baltimore.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Hippodrome_Theatre_(Baltimore)" title="Hippodrome Theatre (Baltimore)">Hippodrome Baltimore</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Baltimore has three state-designated arts and entertainment (A &amp; E) districts. The <a href="/wiki/Station_North_Arts_and_Entertainment_District" title="Station North Arts and Entertainment District">Station North Arts and Entertainment District</a>, <a href="/wiki/Highlandtown_Arts_District,_Baltimore,_MD" title="Highlandtown Arts District, Baltimore, MD">Highlandtown Arts District</a>, and the Bromo Arts &amp; Entertainment District. The Baltimore Office of Promotion &amp; The Arts, a non-profit organization, produces events and arts programs as well as manages several facilities. It is the official Baltimore City Arts Council. BOPA coordinates Baltimore's major events including New Year's Eve and July 4 celebrations at the Inner Harbor, <a href="/wiki/Artscape_(festival)" title="Artscape (festival)">Artscape</a> which is America's largest free arts festival, Baltimore Book Festival, Baltimore Farmers' Market &amp; Bazaar, School 33 Art Center's Open Studio Tour and the Dr. Martin Luther King, Jr. Parade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[195]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Baltimore Symphony Orchestra">Baltimore Symphony Orchestra</a> is an internationally renowned orchestra, founded in 1916 as a publicly funded municipal organization. The current Music Director is <a href="/wiki/Marin_Alsop" title="Marin Alsop">Marin Alsop</a>, a protégé of <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Bernstein" title="Leonard Bernstein">Leonard Bernstein</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Centerstage_(theater)" title="Centerstage (theater)">Centerstage</a> is the premier theater company in the city and a regionally well-respected group. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lyric_Opera_House" title="Lyric Opera House">Lyric Opera House</a> is the home of <a href="/wiki/Lyric_Opera_Baltimore" title="Lyric Opera Baltimore">Lyric Opera Baltimore</a>, which operates there as part of the Patricia and Arthur Modell Performing Arts Center. <a href="/wiki/The_Baltimore_Consort" title="The Baltimore Consort">The Baltimore Consort</a> has been a leading early music ensemble for over twenty-five years. The France-Merrick Performing Arts Center, home of the restored <a href="/wiki/Thomas_W._Lamb" title="Thomas W. Lamb">Thomas W. Lamb</a>-designed <a href="/wiki/Hippodrome_Theatre_(Baltimore)" title="Hippodrome Theatre (Baltimore)">Hippodrome Theatre</a>, has afforded Baltimore the opportunity to become a major regional player in the area of touring Broadway and other performing arts presentations. Renovating Baltimore's historic theatres have become widespread throughout the city such as the <a href="/wiki/Everyman_Theatre,_Baltimore" title="Everyman Theatre, Baltimore">Everyman</a>, Centre, <a href="/wiki/Senator_Theatre" title="Senator Theatre">Senator</a> and most recent <a href="/wiki/Parkway_Theatre_(Baltimore)" title="Parkway Theatre (Baltimore)">Parkway</a> theatre. Other buildings have been reused such as the former <a href="/wiki/Mercantile_Trust_and_Deposit_Company" title="Mercantile Trust and Deposit Company">Mercantile Deposit and Trust</a> Company bank building. It is now the Chesapeake Shakespeare Company Theater.</p>
<p>Baltimore also boasts a wide array of professional (non-touring) and community theater groups. Aside from Center Stage, resident troupes in the city include <a href="/wiki/Everyman_Theatre,_Baltimore" title="Everyman Theatre, Baltimore">Everyman Theatre</a>, Single Carrot Theatre, and Baltimore Theatre Festival. Community theaters in the city include Fells Point Community Theatre and the <a href="/wiki/The_Arena_Players" title="The Arena Players">Arena Players Inc.</a>, which is the nation's oldest continuously operating African American community theater.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[196]</a></sup> In 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Rock_Opera_Society" title="Baltimore Rock Opera Society">Baltimore Rock Opera Society</a>, an all-volunteer theatrical company, launched its first production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[197]</a></sup></p>
<p>Baltimore is home to the <a href="/wiki/Pride_of_Baltimore_Chorus" title="Pride of Baltimore Chorus">Pride of Baltimore Chorus</a>, a three-time international silver medalist women's chorus, affiliated with <a href="/wiki/Sweet_Adelines_International" title="Sweet Adelines International">Sweet Adelines International</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Maryland_State_Boychoir" title="Maryland State Boychoir">Maryland State Boychoir</a> is located in the northeastern Baltimore neighborhood of Mayfield.</p>
<p>Baltimore is the home of non-profit <a href="/wiki/Chamber_music" title="Chamber music">chamber music</a> organization Vivre Musicale. VM won a 2011–2012 award for Adventurous Programming from the <a href="/wiki/American_Society_of_Composers,_Authors_and_Publishers" title="American Society of Composers, Authors and Publishers">American Society of Composers, Authors and Publishers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chamber_Music_America" title="Chamber Music America">Chamber Music America</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[198]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Peabody_Institute" title="Peabody Institute">Peabody Institute</a>, located in the Mount Vernon neighborhood, is the oldest conservatory of music in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kennedy-center1_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-kennedy-center1-202">[199]</a></sup> Established in 1857, it is one of the most prestigious in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kennedy-center1_202-1"><a href="#cite_note-kennedy-center1-202">[199]</a></sup> along with <a href="/wiki/Juilliard_School" title="Juilliard School">Juilliard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastman_School_of_Music" title="Eastman School of Music">Eastman</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Curtis_Institute_of_Music" title="Curtis Institute of Music">Curtis Institute</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Morgan_State_University" title="Morgan State University">Morgan State University</a> Choir is also one of the nation's most prestigious university choral ensembles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[200]</a></sup> The city is home to the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_School_for_the_Arts" title="Baltimore School for the Arts">Baltimore School for the Arts</a>, a public high school in the Mount Vernon neighborhood of Baltimore. The institution is nationally recognized for its success in preparation for students entering music (vocal/instrumental), theatre (acting/theater production), dance, and visual arts.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Baltimore" title="Sports in Baltimore">Sports in Baltimore</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Baseball">Baseball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Baseball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CamdenYards_2005-05-08.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2304" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/CamdenYards_2005-05-08.jpg/250px-CamdenYards_2005-05-08.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/CamdenYards_2005-05-08.jpg/375px-CamdenYards_2005-05-08.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/CamdenYards_2005-05-08.jpg/500px-CamdenYards_2005-05-08.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>

<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CamdenYards_2005-05-08.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Oriole_Park_at_Camden_Yards" title="Oriole Park at Camden Yards">Oriole Park at Camden Yards</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Series_champions" title="List of World Series champions">List of World Series champions</a> and <a href="/wiki/American_League_Championship_Series" title="American League Championship Series">American League Championship Series</a></div>
<p>Baltimore has a long and storied baseball history, including its distinction as the birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Babe_Ruth" title="Babe Ruth">Babe Ruth</a> in 1895. The original <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles_(19th_century)" title="Baltimore Orioles (19th century)">19th century Baltimore Orioles</a> were one of the most successful early franchises, featuring numerous hall of famers during its years from 1882 to 1899. As one of the eight inaugural American League franchises, the Baltimore Orioles played in the AL during the 1901 and 1902 seasons. The team moved to New York City before the 1903 season and was renamed the New York Highlanders, which later became the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a>. Ruth played for the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles_(minor_league)" title="Baltimore Orioles (minor league)">minor league Baltimore Orioles</a> team, which was active from 1903 to 1914. After playing one season in 1915 as the Richmond Climbers, the team returned the following year to Baltimore, where it played as the Orioles until 1953.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[201]</a></sup></p>
<p>The team currently known as the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">Baltimore Orioles</a> has represented Major League Baseball locally since 1954 when the St. Louis Browns moved to the city of Baltimore. The Orioles advanced to the World Series in 1966, 1969, 1970, 1971, 1979 and 1983, winning three times (1966, 1970 and 1983), while making the playoffs all but one year (1972) from 1969 through 1974.</p>
<p>In 1995, local player (and later Hall of Famer) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cal_Ripken,_Jr." title="Cal Ripken, Jr.">Cal Ripken, Jr.</a> broke <a href="/wiki/Lou_Gehrig" title="Lou Gehrig">Lou Gehrig</a>'s streak of 2,130 consecutive games played, for which Ripken was named <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sportsman_of_the_Year" title="Sportsman of the Year">Sportsman of the Year</a> by <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a></i> magazine.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Six former Orioles players, including Ripken (2007), and two of the team's managers have been inducted into the <a href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame and Museum">Baseball Hall of Fame</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Baltimore_Colts" title="History of the Baltimore Colts">History of the Baltimore Colts</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Baltimore_Ravens" title="History of the Baltimore Ravens">History of the Baltimore Ravens</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:M%26T_Bank_Stadium_DoD.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1682" data-file-width="2500" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/M%26T_Bank_Stadium_DoD.jpg/220px-M%26T_Bank_Stadium_DoD.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/M%26T_Bank_Stadium_DoD.jpg/330px-M%26T_Bank_Stadium_DoD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/M%26T_Bank_Stadium_DoD.jpg/440px-M%26T_Bank_Stadium_DoD.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:M%26T_Bank_Stadium_DoD.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/M%26T_Bank_Stadium" title="M&amp;T Bank Stadium">M&amp;T Bank Stadium</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Prior to an NFL team moving to Baltimore, there had been several attempts at a professional football team prior to the 1950s. Most were minor league or <a href="/wiki/Semi-professional" title="Semi-professional">semi-professional</a> teams. The first major league to base a team in Baltimore was the <a href="/wiki/All-America_Football_Conference" title="All-America Football Conference">All-America Football Conference</a> (AAFC), which had a team named the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Colts_(1947%E2%80%9350)" title="Baltimore Colts (1947–50)">Baltimore Colts</a>. The AAFC Colts played for three seasons in the AAFC (1947, 1948, and 1949), and when the AAFC folded following the 1949 season, moved to the NFL for a single year (1950) before going bankrupt. Three years later, the NFL's <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Texans_(NFL)" title="Dallas Texans (NFL)">Dallas Texans</a> would itself fold, and its assets and player contracts purchased by an ownership team headed by Baltimore businessman <a href="/wiki/Carroll_Rosenbloom" title="Carroll Rosenbloom">Carroll Rosenbloom</a>, who moved the team to Baltimore, establishing a new team also named the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Baltimore_Colts" title="History of the Baltimore Colts">Baltimore Colts</a>. During the 1950s and 1960s, the Colts were one of the NFLs more successful franchises, led by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NFL_Hall_of_Fame" title="NFL Hall of Fame">NFL Hall of Fame</a> quarterback <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Unitas" title="Johnny Unitas">Johnny Unitas</a> who set a then-record of 47 consecutive games with a touchdown pass. The Colts advanced to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NFL_Championship" title="NFL Championship">NFL Championship</a> twice (1958 &amp; 1959) and <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">Super Bowl</a> twice (1969 &amp; 1971), winning all except Super Bowl III in 1969. After the 1983 season, the team <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Colts_relocation_to_Indianapolis" title="Baltimore Colts relocation to Indianapolis">left Baltimore for Indianapolis in 1984</a>, where it became the <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis_Colts" title="Indianapolis Colts">Indianapolis Colts</a>.</p>
<p>The NFL returned to Baltimore when the former <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Browns_relocation_controversy" title="Cleveland Browns relocation controversy">Cleveland Browns</a> moved to Baltimore to become the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Ravens" title="Baltimore Ravens">Baltimore Ravens</a> in 1996. Since then, the Ravens won a Super Bowl championship in <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXXV" title="Super Bowl XXXV">2000</a> and <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLVII" title="Super Bowl XLVII">2012</a>, four <a href="/wiki/AFC_North" title="AFC North">AFC North</a> division championships (2003, 2006, 2011 and 2012), and appeared in four <a href="/wiki/AFC_Championship_Game" title="AFC Championship Game">AFC Championship Games</a> (2000, 2008, 2011 and 2012).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_teams_and_events">Other teams and events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Other teams and events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The first professional sports organization in the United States, <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Jockey_Club" title="Maryland Jockey Club">The Maryland Jockey Club</a>, was formed in Baltimore in 1743. <a href="/wiki/Preakness_Stakes" title="Preakness Stakes">Preakness Stakes</a>, the second race in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Triple_Crown_of_Thoroughbred_Racing" title="United States Triple Crown of Thoroughbred Racing">United States Triple Crown of Thoroughbred Racing</a>, has been held every May at <a href="/wiki/Pimlico_Race_Course" title="Pimlico Race Course">Pimlico Race Course</a> in Baltimore since 1873.</p>
<p>College lacrosse is a popular sport in the spring, as the Johns Hopkins Blue Jays men's lacrosse team has won 44 national championships, the most of any program in history. In addition, Loyola University won its first men's NCAA lacrosse championship in 2012.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Blast" title="Baltimore Blast">Baltimore Blast</a> are a professional arena soccer team that play in the <a href="/wiki/Major_Arena_Soccer_League" title="Major Arena Soccer League">Major Arena Soccer League</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Farms_Arena" title="Royal Farms Arena">Royal Farms Arena</a>. The Blast have won 8 championships in various leagues, including the MASL. A previous entity of the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Blast_(1980%E2%80%9392)" title="Baltimore Blast (1980–92)">Blast</a> played in the <a href="/wiki/Major_Indoor_Soccer_League_(1978%E2%80%9392)" title="Major Indoor Soccer League (1978–92)">Major Indoor Soccer League</a> from 1980 to 1992, winning 1 championship.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Blues" title="Baltimore Blues">Baltimore Blues</a> are a semi-professional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rugby_league_football" title="Rugby league football">rugby league</a> club which began competition in the <a href="/wiki/USA_Rugby_League" title="USA Rugby League">USA Rugby League</a> in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[202]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Bohemians" title="Baltimore Bohemians">Baltimore Bohemians</a> are an American <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_(soccer)" title="Football (soccer)">soccer club</a>. They compete in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USL_Premier_Development_League" title="USL Premier Development League">USL Premier Development League</a>, the fourth tier of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Soccer_Pyramid" title="American Soccer Pyramid">American Soccer Pyramid</a>. Their inaugural season started in the spring of 2012.</p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore_Grand_Prix" title="Baltimore Grand Prix">Baltimore Grand Prix</a> debuted along the streets of the Inner Harbor section of the city's downtown on September 2–4, 2011. The event played host to the <a href="/wiki/American_Le_Mans_Series" title="American Le Mans Series">American Le Mans Series</a> on Saturday and the <a href="/wiki/IndyCar_Series" title="IndyCar Series">IndyCar Series</a> on Sunday. Support races from smaller series were also held, including <a href="/wiki/Indy_Lights" title="Indy Lights">Indy Lights</a>. After three consecutive years, on September 13, 2013, it was announced that the event would not be held in 2014 or 2015 due to scheduling conflicts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[203]</a></sup></p>
<p>The athletic equipment company, <a href="/wiki/Under_Armour" title="Under Armour">Under Armour</a> is also based out of Baltimore. Founded in 1996 by <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Plank" title="Kevin Plank">Kevin Plank</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland" title="University of Maryland">University of Maryland</a> alumnus, the company's headquarters are located in Tide Point, adjacent to <a href="/wiki/Fort_McHenry" title="Fort McHenry">Fort McHenry</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Domino_Sugar" title="Domino Sugar">Domino Sugar</a> factory. The <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Marathon" title="Baltimore Marathon">Baltimore Marathon</a> is the flagship race of several races. The marathon begins at the Camden Yards sports complex and travels through many diverse neighborhoods of Baltimore, including the scenic Inner Harbor waterfront area, historic Federal Hill, Fells Point, and Canton, Baltimore. The race then proceeds to other important focal points of the city such as Patterson Park, Clifton Park, Lake Montebello, the Charles Village neighborhood and the western edge of downtown. After winding through 42.195 kilometres (26.219 mi) of Baltimore, the race ends at virtually the same point at which it starts.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_recreation">Parks and recreation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Parks and recreation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The City of Baltimore boasts over 4,900 acres (1,983 ha) of parkland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-City_Profiles:_Baltimore_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-City_Profiles:_Baltimore-207">[204]</a></sup> The Baltimore City Department of Recreation and Parks manages the majority of parks and recreational facilities in the city including <a href="/wiki/Patterson_Park" title="Patterson Park">Patterson Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_Hill_Park" title="Federal Hill Park">Federal Hill Park</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Druid_Hill_Park" title="Druid Hill Park">Druid Hill Park</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[205]</a></sup> The city is also home to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_McHenry_National_Monument_and_Historic_Shrine" title="Fort McHenry National Monument and Historic Shrine">Fort McHenry National Monument and Historic Shrine</a>, a coastal star-shaped fort best known for its role in the War of 1812. As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trust_for_Public_Land" title="Trust for Public Land">The Trust for Public Land</a>, a national land conservation organization, ranks Baltimore 40th among the 75 largest U.S. cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-City_Profiles:_Baltimore_207-1"><a href="#cite_note-City_Profiles:_Baltimore-207">[204]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Baltimore is an <a href="/wiki/Independent_city_(United_States)" title="Independent city (United States)">independent city</a>, and not part of any <a href="/wiki/County_(United_States)" title="County (United States)">county</a>. For most governmental purposes under Maryland law, Baltimore City is treated as a county-level entity. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> uses counties as the basic unit for presentation of statistical information in the United States, and treats Baltimore as a county equivalent for those purposes.</p>
<p>Baltimore has been a <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a> stronghold for over 150 years, with Democrats dominating every level of government. In virtually all elections, the Democratic primary is the real contest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[206]</a></sup> No Republican has won election to the city council since 1939, and no Republican has won the mayor's race since 1963.</p>
<p>The city hosted the first six <a href="/wiki/Democratic_National_Convention" title="Democratic National Convention">Democratic National Conventions</a>, from 1832 through 1852, and hosted the DNC again in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1860_Democratic_National_Convention" title="1860 Democratic National Convention">1860</a>, <a href="/wiki/1872_Democratic_National_Convention" title="1872 Democratic National Convention">1872</a>, and <a href="/wiki/1912_Democratic_National_Convention" title="1912 Democratic National Convention">1912</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[207]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rasmussen_convs_2012_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rasmussen_convs_2012-211">[208]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="City_government">City government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: City government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mayor">Mayor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Mayor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<dl>
<dd><i>For a full list of mayors, see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Baltimore_Mayors" title="List of Baltimore Mayors">List of Baltimore Mayors</a>.</i></dd>
</dl>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sheila_Dixon" title="Sheila Dixon">Sheila Dixon</a> became the first female mayor of Baltimore on January 17, 2007. As the former City Council President, she assumed the office of Mayor when former Mayor <a href="/wiki/Martin_O%27Malley" title="Martin O'Malley">Martin O'Malley</a> took office as Governor of Maryland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[209]</a></sup> On November 6, 2007, Dixon won the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_mayoral_election,_2007" title="Baltimore mayoral election, 2007">Baltimore mayoral election</a>. Mayor Dixon's administration ended less than three years after her election, the result of a criminal investigation that began in 2006 while she was still City Council President. She was convicted on a single misdemeanor charge of <a href="/wiki/Embezzlement" title="Embezzlement">embezzlement</a> on December 1, 2009. A month later, Dixon made an <a href="/wiki/Alford_plea" title="Alford plea">Alford plea</a> to a <a href="/wiki/Perjury" title="Perjury">perjury</a> charge and agreed to resign from office; Maryland, like most states, does not allow convicted felons to hold office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[210]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[211]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Stephanie_Rawlings-Blake" title="Stephanie Rawlings-Blake">Stephanie Rawlings-Blake</a>, who was City Council President at that time, assumed the office of Mayor on February 4, 2010, when Dixon's resignation became effective.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[212]</a></sup> She was elected to a full term in 2011, receiving 84% of the vote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[213]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Catherine_E._Pugh" title="Catherine E. Pugh">Catherine Pugh</a>, who had lost in a primary contest with Rawlings-Blake in 2011, became the Democratic nominee for 2016 and won the mayoral election in 2016 with 57.1% of the vote; Pugh took office as mayor on December 6, 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fritze_217-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fritze-217">[214]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1city_hall_baltimore.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2340" data-file-width="3508" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/1city_hall_baltimore.jpg/250px-1city_hall_baltimore.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/1city_hall_baltimore.jpg/375px-1city_hall_baltimore.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/1city_hall_baltimore.jpg/500px-1city_hall_baltimore.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>

<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1city_hall_baltimore.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Baltimore_City_Hall" title="Baltimore City Hall">Baltimore City Hall</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Baltimore_City_Council">Baltimore City Council</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Baltimore City Council">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Grassroots pressure for reform, voiced as <a href="/wiki/Question_P" title="Question P">Question P</a>, restructured the city council in November 2002, against the will of the mayor, the council president, and the majority of the council. A coalition of union and community groups, organized by the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Community_Organizations_for_Reform_Now" title="Association of Community Organizations for Reform Now">Association of Community Organizations for Reform Now</a> (ACORN), backed the effort.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[215]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_City_Council" title="Baltimore City Council">Baltimore City Council</a> is now made up of 14 single-member districts and one elected at-large council president. <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_C._Young&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bernard C. Young (page does not exist)">Bernard C. "Jack" Young</a> has been the council president since February 2010, when he was unanimously elected by the other council members to replace Stephanie Rawlings-Blake, who had become mayor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[216]</a></sup> Edward Reisinger, the 10th district representative, is the council's current vice president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[217]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_enforcement">Law enforcement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Law enforcement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Police_Department" title="Baltimore Police Department">Baltimore City Police Department</a>, founded 1784 as a "Night City Watch" and day Constables system and later reorganized as a City Department in 1853, with a following reorganization under State of Maryland supervision in 1859, with appointments made by the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Maryland" title="Governor of Maryland">Governor of Maryland</a> after a disturbing period of civic and elections violence with riots in the later part of the decade, is the current primary law enforcement agency serving the citizens of the City of Baltimore. Campus and building security for the city's <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_City_Public_Schools" title="Baltimore City Public Schools">public schools</a> is provided by the Baltimore City Public Schools Police, established in the 1970s.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Transportation_Authority_Police" title="Maryland Transportation Authority Police">Maryland Transportation Authority Police</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Department_of_Transportation" title="Maryland Department of Transportation">Maryland Department of Transportation</a>, (originally established as the Baltimore Harbor Tunnel Police" when opened in 1957) is the primary law enforcement agency on the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_McHenry_Tunnel_Thruway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Fort McHenry Tunnel Thruway (page does not exist)">Fort McHenry Tunnel Thruway</a> (Interstate 95), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore_Harbor_Tunnel_Thruway" title="Baltimore Harbor Tunnel Thruway">Baltimore Harbor Tunnel Thruway</a> (Interstate 895), which go under the Northwest Branch of the <a href="/wiki/Patapsco_River" title="Patapsco River">Patapsco River</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Interstate_395_(Maryland)" title="Interstate 395 (Maryland)">Interstate 395</a>, which has three ramp bridges crossing the Middle Branch of the <a href="/wiki/Patapsco_River" title="Patapsco River">Patapsco River</a> which are under <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Transportation_Authority" title="Maryland Transportation Authority">MdTA</a> jurisdiction, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore-Washington_International_Airport" title="Baltimore-Washington International Airport">Baltimore-Washington International Airport</a>, (BWI) and have limited concurrent jurisdiction with the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Police_Department" title="Baltimore Police Department">Baltimore City Police Department</a> under a "<a href="/wiki/Memorandum_of_understanding" title="Memorandum of understanding">memorandum of understanding</a>".</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1Courthouse_east.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="853" data-file-width="1174" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/1Courthouse_east.JPG/220px-1Courthouse_east.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/1Courthouse_east.JPG/330px-1Courthouse_east.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/1Courthouse_east.JPG/440px-1Courthouse_east.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1Courthouse_east.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/United_States_Post_Office_and_Courthouse_(Baltimore,_Maryland)" title="United States Post Office and Courthouse (Baltimore, Maryland)">Courthouse east</a> is a historic combined post office and Federal courthouse located in <a href="/wiki/Battle_Monument" title="Battle Monument">Battle Monument</a> Square.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Law enforcement on the fleet of transit buses and transit rail systems serving Baltimore is the responsibility of the <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Transit_Administration_Police" title="Maryland Transit Administration Police">Maryland Transit Administration Police</a>, which is part of the Maryland Transit Administration of the state <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Department_of_Transportation" title="Maryland Department of Transportation">Department of Transportation</a>. The MTA Police also share jurisdiction authority with the Baltimore City Police, governed by a memorandum of understanding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[218]</a></sup></p>
<p>As the enforcement arm of the Baltimore circuit and district court system, the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_City_Sheriff%27s_Office_(Maryland)" title="Baltimore City Sheriff's Office (Maryland)">Baltimore City Sheriff's Office</a>, created by state constitutional amendment in 1844, is responsible for the security of city courthouses and property, service of court-ordered writs, protective and peace orders, warrants, tax levies, prisoner transportation and traffic enforcement. Deputy Sheriffs are sworn law enforcement officials, with full arrest authority granted by the constitution of Maryland, the <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Police_and_Correctional_Training_Commission" title="Maryland Police and Correctional Training Commission">Maryland Police and Correctional Training Commission</a> and the Sheriff of the City of Baltimore.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[219]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard" title="United States Coast Guard">United States Coast Guard</a>, operating out of their shipyard and facility (since 1899) at Arundel Cove on <a href="/wiki/Curtis_Creek" title="Curtis Creek">Curtis Creek</a>, (off Pennington Avenue extending to Hawkins Point Road/Fort Smallwood Road) in the <a href="/wiki/Curtis_Bay,_Baltimore" title="Curtis Bay, Baltimore">Curtis Bay</a> section of southern Baltimore City and adjacent northern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anne_Arundel_County" title="Anne Arundel County">Anne Arundel County</a>. The U.S.C.G. also operates and maintains a presence on Baltimore and Maryland waterways in the <a href="/wiki/Patapsco_River" title="Patapsco River">Patapsco River</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay" title="Chesapeake Bay">Chesapeake Bay</a>. "Sector Baltimore" is responsible for commanding law enforcement and search &amp; rescue units as well as aids to navigation.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Baltimore_City_Fire_Department">Baltimore City Fire Department</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Baltimore City Fire Department">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_City_Fire_Department" title="Baltimore City Fire Department">Baltimore City Fire Department</a></div>
<p>The city of Baltimore is protected by the over 1,800 professional firefighters of the Baltimore City Fire Department (BCFD), which was founded in December 1858 and began operating the following year. Replacing several warring independent volunteer companies since the 1770s and the confusion resulting from <a href="/wiki/Know-Nothing_Riot_of_1856" title="Know-Nothing Riot of 1856">a riot</a> involving the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Know-Nothing" title="Know-Nothing">Know-Nothing</a>" political party two years before, the establishment of a unified professional fire fighting force was a major advance in urban governance. The BCFD operates out of 37 fire stations located throughout the city and has a long history and sets of traditions in its various houses and divisions.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="State_government">State government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: State government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_City_Delegation" title="Baltimore City Delegation">Baltimore City Delegation</a></div>
<p>Since the legislative <a href="/wiki/Redistricting" title="Redistricting">redistricting</a> in 2002, Baltimore has had six legislative districts located entirely within its boundaries, giving the city six seats in the 47-member <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Senate" title="Maryland Senate">Maryland Senate</a> and 18 in the 141-member <a href="/wiki/Maryland_House_of_Delegates" title="Maryland House of Delegates">Maryland House of Delegates</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Delegation_223-0"><a href="#cite_note-Delegation-223">[220]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2002_Plan_224-0"><a href="#cite_note-2002_Plan-224">[221]</a></sup> During the previous 10-year period, Baltimore had four legislative districts within the city limits, but four others overlapped the Baltimore County line.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1992_Plan_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-1992_Plan-225">[222]</a></sup> As of January 2011, all of Baltimore's state senators and delegates were Democrats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Delegation_223-1"><a href="#cite_note-Delegation-223">[220]</a></sup> Approval of the next redistricting plan is expected to become effective in time for Maryland's 2012 congressional primary election on February 14, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[223]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="State_agencies">State agencies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: State agencies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_state_agencies_headquartered_in_Baltimore" title="List of state agencies headquartered in Baltimore">List of state agencies headquartered in Baltimore</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Federal_government">Federal government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Federal government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>Three of the state's eight <a href="/wiki/Congressional_district" title="Congressional district">congressional districts</a> include portions of Baltimore: the <a href="/wiki/Maryland%27s_2nd_congressional_district" title="Maryland's 2nd congressional district">2nd</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Ruppersberger" title="Dutch Ruppersberger">Dutch Ruppersberger</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Maryland%27s_3rd_congressional_district" title="Maryland's 3rd congressional district">3rd</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/John_Sarbanes" title="John Sarbanes">John Sarbanes</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/Maryland%27s_7th_congressional_district" title="Maryland's 7th congressional district">7th</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/Elijah_Cummings" title="Elijah Cummings">Elijah Cummings</a>. All three are Democrats; a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Republican_Party" title="United States Republican Party">Republican</a> has not represented a significant portion of Baltimore in Congress since <a href="/wiki/John_Boynton_Philip_Clayton_Hill" title="John Boynton Philip Clayton Hill">John Boynton Philip Clayton Hill</a> represented the 3rd District in 1927, and has not represented any of Baltimore since the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Shore_of_Maryland" title="Eastern Shore of Maryland">Eastern Shore</a>-based 1st District lost its share of Baltimore after the 2000 census; it was represented by Republican <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Gilchrest" title="Wayne Gilchrest">Wayne Gilchrest</a> at the time.</p>
<p>Maryland's senior <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">Senator</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ben_Cardin" title="Ben Cardin">Ben Cardin</a>, is from Baltimore. He is one of three people in the last four decades to have represented the 3rd District before being elected to the Senate. <a href="/wiki/Paul_Sarbanes" title="Paul Sarbanes">Paul Sarbanes</a> represented the 3rd from 1971 until 1977, when he was elected to the first of five terms in the Senate. Sarbanes was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Mikulski" title="Barbara Mikulski">Barbara Mikulski</a>, who represented the 3rd from 1977 to 1987. Mikulski was succeeded by Cardin, who held the seat until handing it to John Sarbanes upon his election to the Senate in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[225]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Postal_Service" title="United States Postal Service">Postal Service</a>'s Baltimore Main Post Office is located at 900 East Fayette Street in the <a href="/wiki/Jonestown,_Baltimore" title="Jonestown, Baltimore">Jonestown</a> area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[226]</a></sup></p>
<p>The national headquarters for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Social_Security_Administration" title="United States Social Security Administration">United States Social Security Administration</a> is located in Woodlawn, just outside of Baltimore.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_high_schools_in_Maryland" title="List of high schools in Maryland">List of high schools in Maryland</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_universities">Colleges and universities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Colleges and universities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Baltimore is the home of numerous places of higher learning, both public and private. 100,000 college students from around the country attend Baltimore City's 12 accredited two-year or four-year colleges and universities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[227]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[228]</a></sup> Among them are:</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Private">Private</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Private">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
